<div id="review_2119214537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2119214537" />
    <a title="Michael Sliter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32440612-michael-sliter"><img alt="Michael Sliter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556844837p2/32440612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2119214537?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Sliter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Sliter" href="/user/show/32440612-michael-sliter">Michael Sliter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2119214537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17031887117712883721">3.5 stars (but I always round up).<br/><br/>I've rarely been so split on a book before. There was a lot to like about The Left Hand of God. The dark, gritty setting (at least during the first third). The deprivation. The interesting, religion-based story, and the somewhat unclear time period. <br/><br/>But, there are a lot of questionable portions of the book. The shifting POVs, sometimes in a single paragraph. The strange mix of the main characters being completely ignorant and yet somehow knowing a great deal abo</span>
  <span id="freeText17031887117712883721" style="display:none">3.5 stars (but I always round up).<br /><br />I've rarely been so split on a book before. There was a lot to like about The Left Hand of God. The dark, gritty setting (at least during the first third). The deprivation. The interesting, religion-based story, and the somewhat unclear time period. <br /><br />But, there are a lot of questionable portions of the book. The shifting POVs, sometimes in a single paragraph. The strange mix of the main characters being completely ignorant and yet somehow knowing a great deal about the world/things they shouldn't understand. And, the characterization of women.<br /><br />Fantasy is rife with female stereotypes. Damsels in distress. Princesses. Fierce warrior women who try, so hard, to spurn conventions. But, in The Left Hand of God, the only two female characters who have more than a couple of lines were completely weak and vapid. One, a girl who lived her whole life in pleasure, has essentially no personality of her own. The other, said to be a "cold woman" rarely seems cold, but rather <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[falls hook line and sinker into the calculated efforts of the main character to manipulate her into falling in love  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And, every woman was beautiful. <br /><br />Even with all this, I read the book to the end and I already bought the second of the series. I think I adapted to the odd narration, and I am interested in the story. So, we will see where book 2 goes!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17031887117712883721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167519613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167519613" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613919-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483904179p2/2613919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167519613?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/2613919-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8523786-the-left-hand-of-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167519613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13154390614944904966">4 Stars<br/><br/>I am giving the book an overall 3 stars as I enjoyed it a great deal more the second time through. This is a flawed first novel, make no mistake about it. It suffers in pacing, in structure, and even in point of view. That being said, the roots of a great author and great story are easily visible through.<br/><br/>Hoffman has created a very dark and dirty world. Fantasist's rule most of this world and this novel. Our young protagonist Thomas Cale is an "Odd" sort of a different type. Without spoile</span>
  <span id="freeText13154390614944904966" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />I am giving the book an overall 3 stars as I enjoyed it a great deal more the second time through. This is a flawed first novel, make no mistake about it. It suffers in pacing, in structure, and even in point of view. That being said, the roots of a great author and great story are easily visible through.<br /><br />Hoffman has created a very dark and dirty world. Fantasist's rule most of this world and this novel. Our young protagonist Thomas Cale is an "Odd" sort of a different type. Without spoilers he is a gifted fighter and swordsman.<br /><br />The writing is uneven but it rises to heights on many occasions.<br /><br /><br />"From deep inside, something in Cale called for protection, begging to be saved: IdrisPukke save me, Leopold Vipond save me, Henri and Kleist save me, Arbell Swan-Neck save me. But he was beyond all help except the help of the man he hated most in all the world. It was Redeemer Bosco who rescued him from the sickening blow and the red blood spilling on the sand; it was the years of violence at his hands, the daily dread and fear—those were what delivered him. Beginning in his chest, the waters of terror began to freeze. As Solomon Solomon quickly circled, the coldness spread downward through Cale’s heart and guts and into his thighs and then his arms. In only a few seconds, like a miraculous drug suppressing an agonizing pain, the old familiar, numbing, lifesaving indifference to fear and death was back. Cale was himself again."<br /><br /><br />"... In the third and final vision, she brought with her a small boy carrying a hawthorn stick, and from the end of that stick dripped vinegar. ‘Look for this child, and when you see him, prepare him for his work. He is the left hand of God, also called the Angel of Death, and he will bring about all these things.’ ”"<br /><br />I reread this so that I can move on to the second book in this series....<br /><br />Recommended!<br /><br />2 Stars<br /><br />I had very high expectations for this novel and was utterly disappointed. I love novels that have heavy religious undertones, and ones that challenge my Christian heritage.<br /><br />This is a supremely flat and shallow novel. The characters are incredibly thin, detached, and border line unlikeable. I am a big fan of Antiheroes but, I found Thomas Cale to be quite dull. The subject matter alone should have been enough to make this into a dark, gritty, and suspenseful novel. It however finds a way to make rape, religious persecution, murder, and mystery into a two dimensional dull story.<br /><br />I did not like this one and skim read through much of it. I probably will not be going on to the next novels in this series.<br /><br />Pass.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13154390614944904966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_731685113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/731685113" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19074825-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594416438p2/19074825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/731685113?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/19074825-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141042374" href="/book/show/7938510-the-left-hand-of-god">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19074825-ian?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer731685113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8232372162348551022"><b>Final Rating: 3.5/10</b><br/><br/>You can read my full length review of this book at my <a href='https://iangregoire.co.uk/2020/05/02/book-review-the-left-hand-of-god-by-paul-hoffman/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <strong>Official Website</strong>
</a>. Below is an overview of my thoughts about it.<br/><br/><u>OVERVIEW</u><br/><em>The Left Hand Of God</em> is a novel that will leave most readers lamenting what could have been. It’s hard to think of a more salient illustration of snatching defeat from the jaws of victory. The story initially begins as an exceptionally well written dark fantasy tale that threatens to turn a well-worn fantasy trope on its head. But then disaster stri</span>
  <span id="freeText8232372162348551022" style="display:none"><b>Final Rating: 3.5/10</b><br /><br />You can read my full length review of this book at my <a href="https://iangregoire.co.uk/2020/05/02/book-review-the-left-hand-of-god-by-paul-hoffman/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <strong>Official Website</strong>
</a>. Below is an overview of my thoughts about it.<br /><br /><u>OVERVIEW</u><br /><em>The Left Hand Of God</em> is a novel that will leave most readers lamenting what could have been. It’s hard to think of a more salient illustration of snatching defeat from the jaws of victory. The story initially begins as an exceptionally well written dark fantasy tale that threatens to turn a well-worn fantasy trope on its head. But then disaster strikes.<br /><br />After the tenth chapter the story inexplicably morphs into an abysmally written parody come romantic comedy. This is, perhaps, one of the most schizophrenic titles you’re ever likely to encounter. It’s almost as if the book was authored by two different people.<br /><br />Anyone looking for a coherent, adult fantasy tale with a strong plot, great characterisation, and well crafted world building should steer clear of this book, as it possesses none of these attributes. Instead, pick up a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17693064-blood-song" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <strong>Blood Song</strong>
</a> by Anthony Ryan which is the book that <em>The Left Hand Of God</em> wishes it was.<br /><br /><br /><b>Subscribe to my author <a href="http://subscribe.iangregoire.co.uk/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Newsletter</a></b><br /><br /><b>Vist my <a href="https://iangregoire.co.uk/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><b>Official Website</b></a> and <a href="https://lonelyboy1977.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Personal Blog</a></b><br /><br /><b>Follow me on social media:<br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/Ian-Gregoire-105808237954836/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://www.last.fm/user/lonelyboy1977" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Last.fm</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/lonelyboy1977/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://lonelyboy1977.tumblr.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lonelyboy1977" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></b></span>

<div id="review_168100172" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168100172" />
    <a title="Kira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4196694-kira"><img alt="Kira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300439707p2/4196694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168100172?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kira" href="/user/show/4196694-kira">Kira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer168100172&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168100172" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9618479753073456840">Marvelous. The Left Hand of God by Paul Hoffman is piece of art. There was no overkill of violence and suspense was constant down to the very last word. The only part of this book which I didn’t like was the cliff-hanger ending. I want the sequel to come to Asia faster! The protagonist, Thomas Cale is described as the cold hallways of a haunted house. He expresses limited emotion and it isn’t until well near the end that he is human. Yet he remains somewhere in between a flat and round character</span>
  <span id="freeText9618479753073456840" style="display:none">Marvelous. The Left Hand of God by Paul Hoffman is piece of art. There was no overkill of violence and suspense was constant down to the very last word. The only part of this book which I didn’t like was the cliff-hanger ending. I want the sequel to come to Asia faster! The protagonist, Thomas Cale is described as the cold hallways of a haunted house. He expresses limited emotion and it isn’t until well near the end that he is human. Yet he remains somewhere in between a flat and round character for there are some brief moments when he does something completely different from his presume personality.<br /><br />Paul uses dualism in his novel to demonstrate the contrast the two opposing worlds. In doing so he allows the reader to relate to the world he creates. For our world and the one is the novel is filled with grey existences. The Redeemers who should be the most pure form of man often beat the acolytes to point of death for trivial matters. Those deaths aren’t usually the quick slice of the throat either. Even Cale the main protagonist displays the darker side of the usual hero quite often. Yet for each deathblow he makes weren’t his actions actually justified? Who decides what is right and what is wrong. Even people today argue about the “system of justice”. For no one knows and has the right to judge what is “wrong”.<br /><br />If life was a tree and its’ branches every path we take twisting and twining, maybe even turning back. What happens when we reach the end? No matter what road we take. Is every road a predetermine sequence of events leading to inescapable doom? Cale seems to be an abuse marionette of fate. For no every good deed he does, it does not go unpunished. No doubt the Left Hand of God is a tragedy equal to that of the Titanic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9618479753073456840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_394432295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/394432295" />
    <a title="JJ DeBenedictis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6087903-jj-debenedictis"><img alt="JJ DeBenedictis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316493255p2/6087903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/394432295?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JJ DeBenedictis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JJ DeBenedictis" href="/user/show/6087903-jj-debenedictis">JJ DeBenedictis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer394432295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16114758981544123956">This is a seriously odd little book. The writing is very good, and the author does a great job of sucker-punching you with the fact this world's mythology is a disturbingly-warped version of Christianity, but it wouldn't be accurate to say I liked the book. The three stars are more because it's so memorable.<br/><br/>The story is intensely cynical, and I can see some readers being delighted by how brutal its view of humanity is and other readers being very put off by the same fact. The book is fairly soph</span>
  <span id="freeText16114758981544123956" style="display:none">This is a seriously odd little book. The writing is very good, and the author does a great job of sucker-punching you with the fact this world's mythology is a disturbingly-warped version of Christianity, but it wouldn't be accurate to say I liked the book. The three stars are more because it's so memorable.<br /><br />The story is intensely cynical, and I can see some readers being delighted by how brutal its view of humanity is and other readers being very put off by the same fact. The book is fairly sophisticated in that the characters do and say things that the reader must interpret, and the author trusts you to be able to keep up. I liked that.<br /><br />I felt a little distant from the protagonist, but that's maybe a good thing, considering he's a fifteen-year-old killing machine who was made that way via sustained and intentional child abuse. He has friends who grew up in the same environment, and their loyalty to one another does most of the work of keeping you on-side with the characters. They do have redeeming qualities, and their harsher personality traits weren't really their fault, so even though they're rather horrifying people, you won't necessarily mind spending time with them.<br /><br />The book has a weak ending, and since I've read the second one in the trilogy, I can tell you that this is because it's really a single story told in three books, not three stand-alone stories with an over-arching plot. You'll have to read all three to get to the story's true resolution.<br /><br />I don't know whether to recommend this book. It's intellectually interesting, and well executed, and it's unique. I didn't really find it enjoyable, but I can totally see another reader loving it immensely. It's definitely a novel for those with a taste for darker tales.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16114758981544123956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1087529088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087529088" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510311895p2/35855553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087529088?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11178176-the-left-hand-of-god">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087529088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12117797091746194965">I have been curious about Paul Hoffman’s The Left Hand of God for a long time, it’s a book that has been on my to-read list from the first time I stumbled upon it. I had high hopes it would be a fantasy series I’d happily devour, but after reading this first book I was disappointed.<br/><br/>The Left Hand of God isn’t the epic fantasy I had been made to believe it was. In fact, the elements that could be considered fantasy, were buried under so many other details that they became irrelevant to the story. </span>
  <span id="freeText12117797091746194965" style="display:none">I have been curious about Paul Hoffman’s The Left Hand of God for a long time, it’s a book that has been on my to-read list from the first time I stumbled upon it. I had high hopes it would be a fantasy series I’d happily devour, but after reading this first book I was disappointed.<br /><br />The Left Hand of God isn’t the epic fantasy I had been made to believe it was. In fact, the elements that could be considered fantasy, were buried under so many other details that they became irrelevant to the story. If I’m being completely honest, the elements that interested me were pushed aside and seemed to be forgotten about. I’m sure they’ll come back in the future books, but it felt like things were introduced and then forgotten about too often with this one and it made it hard to care about what was happening.<br /><br />Mostly, I feel this is because the book was uncertain of what it wanted to be. It tried to include so many elements, and none were handled as well as they could have been. Things were introduced and pushed aside, something else was introduced but it was never taken as far as it could have been, with this pattern repeated throughout.<br /><br />This one certainly had potential, but it failed to deliver.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12117797091746194965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N37JofbbsoyhouGANOnkdXPJqX3GXwoPRtDKl50hNrb8Zz4pPIwDZfxG+6GFH1mw1F7jFatRJ+We/KXW6aZUmg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Unreckoned jewels glow red with a thirst to know everything and should you inadvertently touch one that has lain for more than a few years, it will latch itself onto you with a power few know how to break. This process is insidious and often unnoticeable until it is too late to rectify. In time you will cease to be, and an evil shadow of the dragon whose jewel you have touched will live again in you.\nThe only sure way to reverse this process, or at least halt it, is to conjure up the living flame and reckon the jewel. His hatching at the confluence, when great Rasalene the moon covers Arhelion the sun, must surely mark him for great things. For long ago dragons wrought a deep wrong on the land, and now is come the time to make amends.\n\n----\n\nFirst in the series, The Ballad of Sir Benfro, Dreamwalker sets the stage for an epic fantasy <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5936630974821664370">Note: <i>Paul^^Hoffman</i><br/><br/>Possibly the only novelist of his generation to be born by the light of a paraffin lamp, Paul Hoffman spent much of his childhood on airfields all around the world watching his father – a pioneer of sports parachuting and European Champion – jumping out of aeroplanes. After a long battle with the English educational system which involved avoiding school whenever possible he was </span>
  <span id="freeText5936630974821664370" style="display:none">Note: <i>Paul^^Hoffman</i><br /><br />Possibly the only novelist of his generation to be born by the light of a paraffin lamp, Paul Hoffman spent much of his childhood on airfields all around the world watching his father – a pioneer of sports parachuting and European Champion – jumping out of aeroplanes. After a long battle with the English educational system which involved avoiding school whenever possible he was offered a place to read English at New College, Oxford when no other university would interview him. After graduating he worked in over twenty different jobs, including boardman in a betting shop, messenger boy to a City merchant bank and teacher. He was also senior film censor at the British Board of Film Classification.<br /><br />His first novel, The Wisdom of Crocodiles took thirteen years to write. Among other things it predicted the re-emergence of international terrorism in the 21st Century and the precise nature of the collapse of the world financial system. Part of the novel was made into a film starring Jude Law and Timothy Spall. His second novel, The Golden Age of Censorship, a black comedy based on his experiences as a film censor, was published in 2007. As a screenwriter he has written or co-written three produced films and worked with, among others, Francis Ford Coppola.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5936630974821664370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

To the warrior-monks known as the Redeemers, who rule over massive armies of child slaves, &quot;the last four things&quot; represent the culmination of a faithful life. Death. Judgement. Heaven. Hell. The last four things represent eternal bliss-or endless destruction, permanent chaos, and infinite pain.  Perhaps nowhere are the competing ideas of heaven and hell exhibited more clearly than in the dark and tormented soul of Thomas Cale. Betrayed by his beloved but still marked by a child\'s innocence, possessed of a remarkable aptitude for violence but capable of extreme tenderness, Cale will lead the Redeemers into a battle for nothing less than the fate of the human race. And though his broken heart foretells the bloody trail he will leave in pursuit of a personal peace he can never achieve, a glimmer of hope remains. The question even Cale can\'t answer: When it comes time to decide the fate of the world, to ensure the extermination of humankind or spare it, what will he choose?
